## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate as a function of time and population size, which is the central problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent models like logistic and Gompertz growth.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/biological populations)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth curve)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractal or allometric growth scaling)
- Logistic with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P) (time-dependent intrinsic growth rate)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal environmental variation)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (hyperbolic density dependence)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Gompertz alternative form: dP_dt = P * (c0 - c1 * log(P)) (linear dependence on log-population)
- Delayed logistic proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P * t (proxy for history-dependent effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence of per-capita growth rate (dP_dt/P) on P → logistic-type density dependence with carrying capacity
- Linear dependence of per-capita growth rate on log(P) → Gompertz-type growth dynamics
- Per-capita growth rate that is non-monotonic in P (rises then falls) → Allee effect requiring minimum population
- Fractional power of P in growth term → allometric scaling reflecting metabolic or surface-area constraints
- Ratio form P/(1+cP) → contest competition where resources are divided among individuals
- Product of two linear factors in P → cubic dP/dt indicating bistability or strong Allee effect
- Multiplicative sinusoidal time factor → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth
- Growth rate proportional to P times a decreasing function of P → general density-dependent negative feedback
- Exponential time factor multiplying growth terms → environmental degradation or improvement over time
- Difference of two power-law terms in P (P^a - P^b) → competing anabolic and catabolic biological processes
